<pics>None</pics><response>None</response><gmap_id>0x80dc07ae0c7e8631:0x2e341026009e181f< /gmap_id></record></dataset><record>
< Text>
After reading all of the reviews on this nearby place I decided to give them a try.  Some of the reviews are either fake or extremely mean spirited people.  The place is reasonably clean.  The service was courteous and efficient.  The food was served quickly, 5 minutes to my table after ordering.  I had the tri tip platter with corn bread, and Mac & Cheese.  The tri tip was well cooked and very tender and tasty.  The Mac & Cheese tasted homemade not from a box.  I ordered a side of onion rings which were a bit greasy but tasty and also appeared to be homemade.

Was this the best BBQ I ever had?  No.  Was it the worst, far from it.  It is a small, appears to be family owned place that is trying to make a go of it in overtaxed, over charged rents, and over regulated California.  Give them a break!  I will return, it was tasty and satisfied my BBQ craving tonight.  I wish people would consider the families, employees and the owners of these small places before leaving harsh and mean spirited reviews that are not called for.<//Text>

<rate>2</rate><review>One of my worst dining experiences ever!
TERRIBLE SERVICE / POOR FOOD QUALITY!

I stumbled across this place. It looked inviting and the menu featured a lot of creative options. There was a lunch special, so I thought I would give it a try.

What a mistake!

The cashier informed me there was a 15 minute wait to receive my take-away order. After checking-in on the order multiple times, it actually took them 45 minutes to prepare a simple chicken wrap with a side of hush puppies!

By the time I got the food, I was so hungry I ate pretty quickly.

It turns out that there was a 1/2-inch long, relatively thick chicken bone in the wrap! I almost chocked on it!

The staff here do not seem to put the necessary effort in for customer service and careful preparation of the food.

It's a shame, this place could be really cool if they worked on managing their operations.

The food tasted "alright".. (nothing worth coming back for), but obviously the service and poor food quality (chicken bones still in the meat) are enough reason to avoid this place!< /review>< Resp>

<user_id>108685370139018629938</user_id>< username>
Jay Keyes< /username>
<Date>1574380126711< /Date><rate>4< /rate><Review>The "Mulita de Asada" is what you want to order here. In a mulita, meat is sandwiched with cheese between two corn tortillas and griddled until the cheese melts, somewhat similar to a quesadilla. Unlike a quesataco or vampiro, low heat and grill times are used to melt the cheese in the mulitas to avoid the tortillas from crisping up. The carne asada was finely-chopped and could have been just about any meat, but had a tender texture, and the mixture of meat, cheese, grease, and tortilla took well to Taco Zone's tangy and fragrant light green salsa.

I ordered a "Suadero Taco" as well, but was way less impressed. Here, they use real suadero (a small cut of meat just before a cow's hind legs and above its udders) unlike most other taco operations in L.A. that use brisket, flank, or other cuts of beef. You can usually tell because, unlike brisket, suadero is very difficult to chew and needs to be marinated, simmered in a charola (a stainless steel disc with a raised convex dome), and then chopped into very small pieces to be palatable. A good general rule is that if you can see the grain in the meat, you're not eating actual suadero, you're likely eating brisket or flank steak. If the meat is grainless or chewy, you're probably eating suadero.

Here, the suadero is indeed finely chopped (like the asada), but much chewier. Unlike other real suadero I've had, Taco Zone's did not taste like much; it seemed as if both the flavors and juices had been cooked out of it and it was rendered stiff and dry. I much preferred the carne asada.< /Review>< pics>
[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOhbntxfEqFaJxwnbZhLvLwRUYGP06IkbM3pN2Z=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNE_9F5filKK5kXh37brPEXcdX8Orl0ZD1ULSEB=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMrkiBdyKNsxJ__fjKxiFoKW_H1yaOwpMD6ETuZ=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNg6TAo7cp470GZyvV58uBPW93ZkrmsKW8JcLW6=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNgAqY3WnXUbCGLUwIguYZODtw9ES8qoalUpKlz=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /pics>

<Rate>4</Rate>< review>
This California smog station is very good.  I checked several smog stations near my home (Oxnard, CA) and this one offers the lowest price for a passed smog test and certificate ($45 total).

I was fortunate to be the first line when I drove my car to the station on Monday morning at 9 AM.  The service technician stated that it would take about 20 minutes to have my out of state car inspected.  And it took that long.

There is seating inside the old and somewhat chilly waiting area.  Fortunately, there is a TV and plenty of magazines to read in case you need to wait for a long time.  There is free water, but no snacks as I've read in others' comments.

I recommend this smog station, based on my experience.  I plan to take two other vehicles there when the appropriate time comes.< /review>

Pizza was fresh, cinnamon sticks and garlic parmesan sticks were delicious, always hot, straight from the oven to the buffet table. All the other pizzas as well, staright from the oven. They had a great variety of pizzas. This pies were thin, light, and crunchy!
Salad bar was good, basic, but satisfying. Staff was friendly, helpful, and I liked that they were announcing what pizza was coming out of the oven.

<Review>UPDATE:  the quote Google has chosen is NOT in reference to this facility, but another by the same company. Please read full review! Google, please correct.

This place could be fantastic. COULD. I genuinely like this gym, but its sorely lacking in TLC and effective management.

I give it three stars because they have a pool and awesome amenities like hot tub, cold plunge, sauna, and steam room.

However, they are sorely lacking in maintenance, cleanliness, and overall some very basic things (soap in the bathroom anyone?). If something breaks, don't expect it to be fixed. There's a water fountain in the women's locker room that has been broken and non-functional for well over a month. The door to the sauna is made out of glass and metal (yeah, METAL in a sauna) and the handle has been hastily taped over with foam insulation to keep you from burning yourself. The towels are dingy and old (if you can find any). Clogged drains, broken shower heads, missing hooks and shower curtains, broken mirrors in the workout areas... the list goes on.

Ironically, the brand new club on Meridian is top notch! They have the latest and greatest equipment and sparkling facilities. No pool and spa style locker rooms though.

It's clear that Fitness Evolution's corporate offices has dedicated all their resources to this new facility. But when you leave your "Elite" location in such disarray, that's simply poor business practices. All we want is for things to actually work and be clean. That's not asking for much.

You are only as strong as your weakest link.<//Review><name>Carmen L. Perez-Seda< /name>< Resp>

<user_id>105949090932604625860< /user_id><user_name>Hunter C. Swart< /user_name>< time>

<Rate>3<//Rate><review>Member since 27 November AD-2015

[86 days]

Located adjacent to the First Unitarian Church of San Jose, and across the street from Saint James Park, is the Masonic Lodge built in the 1924th year of our Lord. As of the time which this synopsis was written the building is owned by Mr. Barry Swenson, who counts Gold's Gym as a lessee: Fitness Evolution is a subsidiary of that corporation.

The cost is approximately $43/month, which is drastically less than could be expected considering the potential clientele. Potential downsides are that the organization is not in control of the lease (assumption), there is riffraff which brings a low-class element, and as has been mentioned in previous reviews there are some things that are to be desired, although during February 2016 there are renovations to the locker-rooms which suggest a gradual update is being implemented or phased in.

The other gymnasium which bears the same name in the immediate vicinity is significantly smaller and without the novel amenities which are particular to this location. Said features include the Pool (consisting of 5 lanes), the Sauna & Steam Room (a set of 2), a Massage room, plenty of space for relaxing poolside (e.g., outdoor space which is fenced off with a high wall), and the basketball court which is part of the eastern section of the facility (an add-on from the original temple complex).

The staff does not espouse animosity or duplicity, and is consistently professional. Although relatively young (taken as a mean), the haughty air that had plagued the previous establishment is absent: they are courteous and make an effort to welcome persons with more than a modicum of sincerity.</review><pics>None< /pics><Resp>None< /Resp>< gmapID>

This has been our local cinema for the last year, and we've come here about 5-7 times since moving to San Mateo. The cinema itself plays all the latest blockbusters, so the range of fares isn't very extensive if your taste runs to foreign/indie. That said, it is very adequate.
